      "body": "**Description of the bug**\r\nWhen the title of a comic issue contains \"Chapter #\", the scanner uses the chapter number as the issue number rather than the actual issue number from the filename. The issue is marked as missing rather than complete.\r\n\r\n**To Reproduce**\r\n1. Add \"The Mandalorian, Vol2 (2023)\" to the library\r\n2. Add file to comic directory\r\nexample: 'Star Wars The Mandalorian (2023) - v02 - Issue 001 - Chapter 9 Redemption.cbz'\r\n\r\n3. From the GUI, click the Refresh & Scan button\r\n4. Debug output is: \r\n[Task Handler][DEBUG] Extracting filename data: /comics/Star Wars The Mandalorian/Volume 02 (2023)/Star Wars The Mandalorian (2023) - v02 - **Issue 001** - Chapter 9 Redemption.cbz\r\n[Task Handler][DEBUG] Extracting filename data: {'series': 'Star Wars The Mandalorian', 'year': 2023, 'volume_number': 2, 'special_version': None, **'issue_number': 9.0**, 'annual': False}\r\n\r\n5. If you use remove the \"Chapter 9\" from the filename, the correct issue number is used and the issue marked as complete. However, if the system renames the file using the issue title, \"Chapter 9\" is added back into the filename and the issue is subsequently re-marked as missing.\r\n\r\n**Expected behaviour**\r\nThe name scanner should use the \"Issue #\" as the issue number rather than the \"Chapter #\" and mark the issue as complete.\r\n\r\n**Version info**\r\nAbout\r\n\r\nKapowarr version\tv1.0.0-beta-3\r\nPython version\t3.8.17.final.0\r\nDatabase version\t10\r\nDatabase location\t/app/db/Kapowarr.db\r\nData folder\t/app\r\n\r\nKapowarr is running in a Docker container on Ubuntu 22.04.\r\nClient is MacOS 14.1.1, using Safari 17.1. Issue persists regardless of client/browser combination.\r\n\r\n",

The actual function implementation is not important here:\r\n```\r\ndef handle_input(input_instance: SimpleModel) -> None:\r\n    pass\r\n```\r\n\r\nIn order to do so, I would like to use the `coverage()` function of pydantic `ModelFactory` as such:\r\n```\r\ndef test_handle_input(self):\r\n    model_generator = SimpleModelFactory.coverage()\r\n\r\n    for model in model_generator:\r\n        handle_input(model)\r\n```\r\n\r\nThis test, when called, returns a `TypeError` exception at line `for model in model_generator`.\r\n\r\nHowever, it works very well with a pydantic model defined as follows:\r\n```\r\nclass SimpleModel(BaseModel):\r\n    a: int\r\n    b: float\r\n    c: str\r\n    d: Union[bool, int]\r\n```\r\n\r\nI expected `ModelFactory` to work for all cases where `None` is a valid value (e.g. `Optional[int]`, `Union[NoneType, int, float]`, etc.) but it seems that, for now, either it is not a feature polyfactory wants to handle or there is a bug in the code base.\n\n### URL to code causing the issue\n\n_No response_\n\n### MCVE\n\n```python\nfrom typing import Optional\r\n\r\nfrom polyfactory.factories.pydantic_factory import ModelFactory\r\nfrom pydantic import BaseModel\r\n\r\nclass SimpleModel(BaseModel):\r\n    a: int\r\n    b: float\r\n    c: str\r\n    d: Optional[bool]\r\n\r\nclass SimpleModelFactory(ModelFactory[SimpleModel]):\r\n    __model__ = SimpleModel\r\n\r\nfor model in SimpleModelFactory.coverage():\r\n    print(model)\n```\n\n\n### Steps to reproduce\n\n```bash\n1.
